J\n\n3\'13\n\n!\n,\n~\n\nI\n\nf\n\n"""- -- ---Tnn \'" ",. T. I\n\n~a~ lR\n\n"\'\n\n....\n\n-,\nI\n\n,\n\n!\n\n1.0 SUMMARY\nThis paper documents the results of an analysis conducted to determine\nspace shuttle vehicle (SSV) subsystem margins for the reference flight profile (reference 1) for the first orbital flight test (OFT-1). The objective\nof this assessment was to determine the "benigness" of the candidate OFT-l\nlaunch trajectory in the presence of winds, environment and system dispersions, and aerodynamic uncertainties. In particular, this analysis attempted\nto answer the following question. "Can the SSV fly the OFT-l ascent safely\n(i.e., with adequate subsystems margins) in the presence of dispersions,\nincluding aerodynamic variations?"\n\n......\n\nIn general, the results of this analysis show increased margins for the\nOFT-l indicators when compared to Mission 3A results. The inclusion of\nelement and wing aerodynamic variations on OFT-1, in combination with winds\nand systems dispersions, resulted in the fot~ard Z (FT01) attach load\nindicator exceeding specified "limits". The inboard and outboard e1evon\nhinge moment margins (9 percent and 3 percent, respectively) on OFT-1 reflect\nvalues consistent with the load relief requirements dictated by e1evon hinge\nmoment variations. All other structural load indicators for OFT-l had margins in excess of 10 percent.\nThe SSV first stage stagnation heating indicators for OFT-1 were about\n45 percent less than for Mission 3A. The hydraulic systems demands for both\nmissions were essentially the same.\nThe results of this analysis also show OFT-l performance reqUirements\nfrom the consideration of winds and dispersions to be approximately 3,300 lbs\ngreater than Mission 3A.\n2.0 INTRODUCTION\nThe orbital flight test (OFT) phase of the Space Shuttle Program currently consists of six orbital flights beginning in March 1979. The primary\npurpose of the OFT Program is to demonstrate and verify SSV systems and\nflight capabilities by satisfying various flight test requirements. As a\nresult of the uniqueness of the SSV system and the various unknowns associated with the ascent environment, subsystem requirements have been established to insure as \'fbenign" an ascent as possible for OFT-l.\nThe purpose of this study is to identify the minimum margin on each\nsubsystem which results from flying the OFT-l ascent in the design environment. Data are given which compare several vehicle and trajectory parameters\nfor OFT-l with the corresponding Mission 3A results. The impact of winds and\ndispersions on OFT-l and Mission 3A structural load indicator margins is\nincluded in this analysis. Also, included in this assessment was the impact\nof wind criteria and maximum nominal dynamic pressure on OFT-l margins (see\nAppendices A and B).\n1\n\n!\n\nl-\n\n-;\n\nI\n\n!\ni\n\n~, ~\' __~\'~h_~MH_\xc2\xb7ct~~~w~~_-~_"__~~______________~__________________________~~~______-==========\n\n1\n,I\n""~~\n\nri\n\nl"\nf,..\n\n1\' . \xe2\x80\xa2-\n\ntf!\n\nI\n\n3.0 METHOD OF ANALYSIS\ndegree-ofAll trajec torie s for this analysis were computed using a 6of a rigid\nof motion\nfreedom trajec tory program integ rating the equations\nnce of\nbody moving over a rotati ng oblate spheroid planet under the influe analy sis,\nses of this\npurpo\nthrus t, gravi ty, and aerodynamic forces. "\' T\n\nThe impact of the RSS of the dispersions considered on the LOX bulkhead\nload indicator and first stage heating is given in figure 158. The RSS of\nsubsystem and aerodynamic dispersions (hot SRB being the major contributor)\naccounted for about a 5 percent reduction in LOX bulkhead load indicator\nmargin. By combining these dispersions with the worst case winds, an\noverall margin of 11 percent and 8 percent results for Mission 3A and OFT-l\nrespectively. As shown, the RSS of the dispersions resulted in about a + 20\npercent variation in the maximum first stage convective heat rate on both\nOFT-l and Mission 3A. The maximum variation in first stage heat load was\nabout + 15 percent for both OFT-l and Mission 3A. By combining the worst\nheadwind with the RSS of the \'dispersions, it is possible to determine that\nthe maximum expected heat rate for OFT-l is 45.6 percent lower than for\nMission 3A. Similarly, the maximum expected heat load is 43.6 percent\nlower. As seen in figure 158, the maximum dynamic pressure variation due to\ndispersions on OFT-l is about 15 percent larger than for Mission 3A. The\ncombined impact of worst case dispersions with worst case wind direction\n(95 percentile headwind) on flutter margin is presented in figure 159 for\nMissions 3A and OFT-l. As shown, the minimum expected flutter margin for\nMission 3A would be 7 percent, while for OFT-l that margin would be 20 percent.\n\n_.\n\nFJr the purposes of this analysis, SRB staging conditions were assessed\nwith the same dispersions considered in the maximum dynamic pressure flight\nregime with the exception that SRB web action time dispersion was replaced\nwith SRB thrust mismatch. Figure 160 gives the SRB staging conditions which\nresult from the worst case SRB mismatch for Missions 3A and OFT-l. The\nimpact of the RSS of all dispersions on staging conditions is summarized in\nfigure 161. As indicated by these results, the baseline flight control\nsystem (FCS 8) would not require a separation inhibit to achieve acceptable\nSRB staging initial conditions.\n\nI\n\n1\n\nI\nI\n\nExcept for SRB thrust mismatch, the dispersions considered in this\nanalysis had negligible impact on the SSV hydraulic system demands. The\nhydraulic flow demands produced by the worst case mismatch dispersions are\ngiven in figures 162 and 163 for OFT-1 and Mission 3A. The flow required\n(approximately 40 gpm pre-staging and 50 gpm post-staging) by these dis- .\npersions is well within the capability of the SSV hydraulic system.\n\n1\n\nI\n\nThe effect of the RSS of the dispersions on SSV injected weight is\ngiven in figure 164 for OFT-l and Mission 3A. As shown, the maximum required propellantforOFT-l exceeds the 5,200 lbs currently allotted as flight\nperformance reserve.\xc2\xb7 The significantly larger variation in performance on\nOFT-l indicates a need for an FPR assessment specifically for OFT-l as the\nuse of 3A reserves will not be adequate.\n\n1\n\n4.3.2 ELEMENT AERODYNAMICS\n\nI\n\nJ\n\nj\n.~\n\nj\n\nI\n\nTo this point, the discussion in this section has dealt with the overall impact on vehicle and trajectory parameters of an RSS combination of\n\n1\n\n7\n\nJ\n1\n\n!\n\n.\n\nu\n\nI!\n\nsubsystem dispersions. In addition to these dispersions, this analysis\nincluded an assessment of element aerodynamic coefficient tolerances\n(Mission 3A) and variations (OFT-l). Each element dispersion was considered\nindividually with their collective impact identified by root sum squaring\neach tolerance or variation delta.\nWhen the appropriate elevon hinge moment uncertainties were considered\nin trajectory simulations, outboard elevon load relief was required with\npositive outboard elevon hinge moment tolerances (3A) and variations (OFT-l).\nSimi 1arly, the only requirement for inboard elevon load rel i.ef resulted from\nnegative inboard elevon hinge moment variations on OFT-l. Figures 165 - 168\npresent the e1evon deflections and hinge moments which resulted from flying\nthe nominal Mission 3A and OFT-l trajectory profiles with hinge moment tolerances and variations, respectively. As seen from these results, approximately 3\xc2\xb0 of outboard elevon deflection for load relief was required with\nMission 3A tolerances and OFT-1 variations. While 3 to 8 degrees of inboard\nelevon deflection for load relief was required on OFT-l, no load relief was\nnecessary on Mission 3A.\n\n--\n\nFigures 169 - 185 give the impact of element aerodynamic toleY\'ances\n(Mission 3A) and variations (OFT-1) on the SSV structural load indicator\nmargins. Figures 186 and 187 summarize the minimum margins which result\nfrom the consideration of element aerodynamic dispersions for Missions 3A\nand OFT-l, respectively. As shown, the inboard and outboard e1evon hinge\nmoments and FT01 are the only structural load indicatrs which have margins\nreduced to below 20 percent as a result of element aerodynamic tolerances\n(3A) or variations (OFT-1). It should be pointed out that element aerodynamic tolerances and variations were found to have negligible impact on SSV\nmaximum dynamic pressure, heating, SRB staging conditions, hydraulic requirements, or performance.\n\nI\nj\n\n5.0 CONCLUSIONS\n5.1\nI\':\n\n,\n,\n\n,\n\n;\n\nSTRUCTURAL LOAD INDICATORS\n\nFigures 190 - 206 give the minimum margin as a function of Mach number\nwhich results from root sum squaring the mean wind value of each structural\nload indicator with the resultant delta from inflight winds, system dispersions, and element aerodynamic dispersions. As such, a and a effects on vehicle heating are not\naccounted for in these results.\n5. 4 HYDRAULI CS\nSRB thrust mismatch was the only environment or system dispersion-which\nwas found to significantly affect SSV hydraulic flow demands in the first\nstage. On both OFT-l and Mission 3A this dispersion required about 70 percent of the hydraulic system flow capability just prior to SRB separation.\nFor all other environment and system dispersions, the vertical rise and tilt\nflight regime has the highest hydraulic flow requirements, approximately\n15 gpm (about 25 percent Df the capability).\n5.5 SRB SEPARATION\nOFT-l and Mission 3A launch trajectory simulations using baseline FCS 8\nand a worst case combination of winds and dispersions (including SRB thrust\nmismatch) resulted in SRB staging conditions within the range of acceptable\nSRB separation initial conditions identified in reference 15 without the need\nfor a separation delay.\n5.6 INJECTED WEIGHT\nThe worst case combination of winds and dispersions resulted in a maximum SSV injected weight reduction of 5,200 lbs on Mission 3A and 8,550 lbs on\nOFT-l. This reduction in performance exceeds the 5,200 lbs which is currently allotted for FPR on OFT-l. Also, the large performance variation noted\non OFT-l due to winds (+1,500 lbs to -3,600 lbs, figure 132) indicates the\nneed for an investigation of OFT-l trajectory shaping criteria. The large\nvariation of OFT-l performance due to dispersions (figure 164) indicates the\nneed for an OFT~l FPR assessment.\n\ni\ni\n\nj\n\nj\n\n5.7 GENERAL\n\n1\n\nBased on the results presented in this anal\xc2\xa5sis (with appropriate\nconsideration given to the aerodynamic data base), a change in the outboard\nelevon schedule is indicated. By changing the nominal ,schedule in the\nM= 1.05 to M = 1.25 region to slightly more positive deflection, the likelihood of outboard elevon hinge moment deflection for load relief due to\nwinds or aerodynamic uncertainties will be reduced with only a minor impact\non other load indicators and vehicle performance.\n\nI\n\nJ\n\n1\n\nr\n10\n\nI\n\nI\n\nI\n.\n\xe2\x80\xa2\n\nThe sensitivity of the wing bending, shear, and FTOl structural load\nindicators to variations in inf1ight winds indicates a potential for updating\nthe nominal ascent profile for both Missions 3A and OFT-l. By biasing the\nfirst stage ascent for a somewhat less negative Qa in the maximum dynamic\npressure region (M = 1.5) it is possible to increase the FT01 indicator margin. However, since some reduction in wing root bending and wing shear\nmargins will result, such a biasing update should only be considered within\nthe context of the acceptability of the aerodynamic data base (IVBC-2) and\nthe structural load indicator limits (reference 9) used in this analysis .\nWhile the need for an FPR assessment for OFT-l ha~ already been established, the OFT-1 flight azimuth (for tracking) and main engine cutoff (MECO)\n(entry crossrange) constraints preclude a significant reduction in the sensitivity of OFT-1 vehicle performance to winds.\n\n;-.,\n\nOverall, with due consideration given to the RSS combination of worst\ncase winds with SSV system dispersions and aerodynamic variations, the\nresults of this analysis indicate adequate margin on the vehicle subsystems\nfor OFT -1.\n6.0\n\nSYMBOLS\n\nF SSME\nHMI\n\ninboard elevon hinge moment, in-lbs\n\nHMO\n\noutboard elevon hinge moment, in-lbs\n\nHYDILD\n,\n\nspace shuttle main engine thrust, actual,
